If `overwrite_input` is ``True`` and `a` is not already an\n3944:        `ndarray`, an error will be raised.\n3945:     keepdims : bool, optional\n3946:         If this is set to True, the axes which are reduced are left\n3947:         in the result as dimensions with size one. With this option,\n3948:         the result will broadcast correctly against the original `arr`.\n3949: \n3950:     Returns\n3951:     -------\n3952:     median : ndarray\n3953:         A new array holding the result. If the input contains integers\n3954:         or floats smaller than ``float64``, then the output data-type is\n3955:         ``np.float64``.  Otherwise, the data-type of the output is the\n3956:         same as that of the input. If `out` is specified, that array is\n3957:         returned instead.\n3958: \n3959:     See Also\n3960:     --------\n3961:     mean, percentile\n3962: \n3963:     Notes\n3964:     -----\n3965:     Given a vector ``V`` of length ``N``, the median of ``V`` is the\n3966:     middle value of a sorted copy of ``V``, ``V_sorted`` - i\n3967:     e., ``V_sorted[(N-1)/2]``, when ``N`` is odd, and the average of the\n3968:     two middle values of ``V_sorted`` when ``N`` is even.\n3969: \n3970:     Examples\n3971:     --------\n3972:     >>> import numpy as np\n3973:     >>> a = np.array([[10, 7, 4], [3, 2, 1]])\n3974:     >>> a\n3975:     array([[10,  7,  4],\n3976:            [ 3,  2,  1]])\n3977:     >>> np.median(a)\n3978:     np.float64(3.5)\n3979:     >>> np.median(a, axis=0)\n3980:     array([6.5, 4.5, 2.5])\n3981:     >>> np.median(a, axis=1)\n3982:     array([7.,  2.])\n3983:     >>> np.median(a, axis=(0, 1))\n3984:     np.float64(3.5)\n3985:     >>> m = np.median(a, axis=0)\n3986:     >>> out = np.zeros_like(m)\n3987:     >>> np.median(a, axis=0, out=m)\n3988:     array([6.5,  4.5,  2.5])\n3989:     >>> m\n3990:     array([6.5,  4.5,  2.5])\n3991:     >>> b = a.copy()\n3992:     >>> np.median(b, axis=1, overwrite_input=True)\n3993:     array([7.,  2.])\n3994:     >>> assert not np.all(a==b)\n3995:     >>> b = a.copy()\n3996:     >>> np.median(b, axis=None, overwrite_input=True)\n3997:     np.float64(3.5)\n3998:     >>> assert not np.all(a==b)\n3999: \n4000:     \"\"\"\n4001: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/numpy--v2.2.2@9ca88bff35bf60de74f9f95e6f90e6b4e0913e78/-/blob/numpy/lib/_function_base_impl.py%3FL3900-4000"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_018MuPYsK24YyTizvriCuJqi","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_018tjx1MdKjNkx2UmgbWYfCX","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/numpy/lib/_rolling_median_impl.py","content":"\"\"\"\nRolling median implementation for 1-D arrays.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport functools\nimport numpy as np\nfrom numpy._core import overrides\nfrom numpy._core.numeric import asarray, asanyarray\n\n__all__ = ['rolling_median']\n\narray_function_dispatch = functools.partial(\n    overrides.array_function_dispatch, module='numpy')\n\n\ndef _rolling_median_dispatcher(a, window_size, axis=None, mode=None):\n    return (a,)\n\n\n@array_function_dispatch(_rolling_median_dispatcher)\ndef rolling_median(a, window_size, *, axis=-1, mode='valid'):\n    \"\"\"\n    Compute a rolling median along the given axis.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    a : array_like\n        Input array or object that can be converted to an array.\n    window_size : int\n        Size of the rolling window. Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output shape based on the window size and input array size:\n\n        'valid':\n            Output will have size max(N - window_size + 1, 0) where N is the\n            size along the given axis. This is the default mode.\n        'same':\n            Output will have the same shape as the input along the given axis.\n        'full':\n            Output will have size N + window_size - 1 where N is the size\n            along the given axis.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians. The output array has the same dtype as the\n        input array (or float64 for integer inputs less than 64-bit).\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    numpy.lib.stride_tricks.sliding_window_view : Create sliding windows.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed using a sliding window of the specified size.\n    For each window position, the median of the values in that window is computed.\n\n    The function handles edge cases as follows:\n    - If window_size is 1, the output is simply the input (in 'same' mode) or\n      a view of the input (in 'valid' or 'full' modes).\n    - If window_size is larger than the array size:\n      - 'valid' mode returns an empty array\n      - 'same' mode returns an array with NaN values\n      - 'full' mode returns the single median of the entire array\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 3, 6, 4, 5, 2])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([3., 4., 4., 4.])\n\n    >>> a = np.array([[1, 2, 3, 4],\n    ...               [5, 6, 7, 8]])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 2, axis=1)\n    array([[1.5, 2.5, 3.5],\n           [5.5, 6.5, 7.5]])\n\n    For 'same' mode, the output has the same shape as the input:\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([[1., 2., 3., 4.],\n           [5., 6., 7., 8.]])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asanyarray(a)\n\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if axis is None:\n        a = a.ravel()\n        axis = 0\n\n    axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\n\n    # Get the size along the specified axis\n    n = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Handle window_size larger than array\n    if window_size > n:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            # Return empty array with appropriate shape\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = 0\n            return np.empty(tuple(shape), dtype=a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            # Return array filled with NaN\n            return np.full(a.shape, np.nan, dtype=float)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Return single median value\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = window_size - n + 1\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Compute median of the entire array along axis\n            med = np.median(a, axis=axis, keepdims=True)\n            # Reshape the result to have the window_size - n + 1 elements\n            return np.broadcast_to(med, tuple(shape))\n\n    # Special case: window_size = 1\n    if window_size == 1:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a.astype(float if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Pad with NaN values\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = n\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Place the original values in the middle\n            slices = [slice(None)] * a.ndim\n            slices[axis] = slice(0, n)\n            result[tuple(slices)] = a\n            return result\n\n    # Compute rolling median using stride tricks\n    from numpy.lib.stride_tricks import sliding_window_view\n\n    # Create a sliding window view\n    windowed = sliding_window_view(a, window_size, axis=axis)\n\n    # The sliding_window_view adds a new axis at the end for the window\n    # We need to compute median along that axis\n    # The shape of windowed is: original_shape[:axis] + (n - window_size + 1,) + original_shape[axis+1:] + (window_size,)\n\n    # Move the window axis to be the last axis and compute median\n    window_axis = windowed.ndim - 1\n    result = np.median(windowed, axis=window_axis)\n\n    # Handle different modes\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return result\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        # Pad the result to have the same size as the input\n        pad_total = n - (n - window_size + 1)\n        pad_before = window_size // 2\n        pad_after = pad_total - pad_before\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        # Pad the result to have size n + window_size - 1\n        pad_total = window_size - 1\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = 0\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1337,"cache_read_input_tokens":49531,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1337},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"44b1cb17-e026-48fe-a993-849ae447862e","uuid":"97945917-b299-473f-9082-bde437c6d905"}

Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output shape based on the window size and input array size:\n\n        'valid':\n            Output will have size max(N - window_size + 1, 0) where N is the\n            size along the given axis. This is the default mode.\n        'same':\n            Output will have the same shape as the input along the given axis.\n        'full':\n            Output will have size N + window_size - 1 where N is the size\n            along the given axis.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians. The output array has the same dtype as the\n        input array (or float64 for integer inputs less than 64-bit).\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    numpy.lib.stride_tricks.sliding_window_view : Create sliding windows.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed using a sliding window of the specified size.\n    For each window position, the median of the values in that window is computed.\n\n    The function handles edge cases as follows:\n    - If window_size is 1, the output is simply the input (in 'same' mode) or\n      a view of the input (in 'valid' or 'full' modes).\n    - If window_size is larger than the array size:\n      - 'valid' mode returns an empty array\n      - 'same' mode returns an array with NaN values\n      - 'full' mode returns the single median of the entire array\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 3, 6, 4, 5, 2])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([3., 4., 4., 4.])\n\n    >>> a = np.array([[1, 2, 3, 4],\n    ...               [5, 6, 7, 8]])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 2, axis=1)\n    array([[1.5, 2.5, 3.5],\n           [5.5, 6.5, 7.5]])\n\n    For 'same' mode, the output has the same shape as the input:\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([[1., 2., 3., 4.],\n           [5., 6., 7., 8.]])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asanyarray(a)\n\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if axis is None:\n        a = a.ravel()\n        axis = 0\n\n    axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\n\n    # Get the size along the specified axis\n    n = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Handle window_size larger than array\n    if window_size > n:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            # Return empty array with appropriate shape\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = 0\n            return np.empty(tuple(shape), dtype=a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            # Return array filled with NaN\n            return np.full(a.shape, np.nan, dtype=float)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Return single median value\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = window_size - n + 1\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Compute median of the entire array along axis\n            med = np.median(a, axis=axis, keepdims=True)\n            # Reshape the result to have the window_size - n + 1 elements\n            return np.broadcast_to(med, tuple(shape))\n\n    # Special case: window_size = 1\n    if window_size == 1:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a.astype(float if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Pad with NaN values\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = n\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Place the original values in the middle\n            slices = [slice(None)] * a.ndim\n            slices[axis] = slice(0, n)\n            result[tuple(slices)] = a\n            return result\n\n    # Compute rolling median using stride tricks\n    from numpy.lib.stride_tricks import sliding_window_view\n\n    # Create a sliding window view\n    windowed = sliding_window_view(a, window_size, axis=axis)\n\n    # The sliding_window_view adds a new axis at the end for the window\n    # We need to compute median along that axis\n    # The shape of windowed is: original_shape[:axis] + (n - window_size + 1,) + original_shape[axis+1:] + (window_size,)\n\n    # Move the window axis to be the last axis and compute median\n    window_axis = windowed.ndim - 1\n    result = np.median(windowed, axis=window_axis)\n\n    # Handle different modes\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return result\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        # Pad the result to have the same size as the input\n        pad_total = n - (n - window_size + 1)\n        pad_before = window_size // 2\n        pad_after = pad_total - pad_before\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        # Pad the result to have size n + window_size - 1\n        pad_total = window_size - 1\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = 0\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output shape based on the window size and input array size:\n\n        'valid':\n            Output will have size max(N - window_size + 1, 0) where N is the\n            size along the given axis. This is the default mode.\n        'same':\n            Output will have the same shape as the input along the given axis.\n        'full':\n            Output will have size N + window_size - 1 where N is the size\n            along the given axis.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians. The output array has the same dtype as the\n        input array (or float64 for integer inputs less than 64-bit).\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    numpy.lib.stride_tricks.sliding_window_view : Create sliding windows.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed using a sliding window of the specified size.\n    For each window position, the median of the values in that window is computed.\n\n    The function handles edge cases as follows:\n    - If window_size is 1, the output is simply the input (in 'same' mode) or\n      a view of the input (in 'valid' or 'full' modes).\n    - If window_size is larger than the array size:\n      - 'valid' mode returns an empty array\n      - 'same' mode returns an array with NaN values\n      - 'full' mode returns the single median of the entire array\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 3, 6, 4, 5, 2])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([3., 4., 4., 4.])\n\n    >>> a = np.array([[1, 2, 3, 4],\n    ...               [5, 6, 7, 8]])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 2, axis=1)\n    array([[1.5, 2.5, 3.5],\n           [5.5, 6.5, 7.5]])\n\n    For 'same' mode, the output has the same shape as the input:\n\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([[1., 2., 3., 4.],\n           [5., 6., 7., 8.]])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = asanyarray(a)\n\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if axis is None:\n        a = a.ravel()\n        axis = 0\n\n    axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\n\n    # Get the size along the specified axis\n    n = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Handle window_size larger than array\n    if window_size > n:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            # Return empty array with appropriate shape\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = 0\n            return np.empty(tuple(shape), dtype=a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            # Return array filled with NaN\n            return np.full(a.shape, np.nan, dtype=float)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Return single median value\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = window_size - n + 1\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Compute median of the entire array along axis\n            med = np.median(a, axis=axis, keepdims=True)\n            # Reshape the result to have the window_size - n + 1 elements\n            return np.broadcast_to(med, tuple(shape))\n\n    # Special case: window_size = 1\n    if window_size == 1:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a.astype(float if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Pad with NaN values\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = n\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Place the original values in the middle\n            slices = [slice(None)] * a.ndim\n            slices[axis] = slice(0, n)\n            result[tuple(slices)] = a\n            return result\n\n    # Compute rolling median using stride tricks\n    from numpy.lib.stride_tricks import sliding_window_view\n\n    # Create a sliding window view\n    windowed = sliding_window_view(a, window_size, axis=axis)\n\n    # The sliding_window_view adds a new axis at the end for the window\n    # We need to compute median along that axis\n    # The shape of windowed is: original_shape[:axis] + (n - window_size + 1,) + original_shape[axis+1:] + (window_size,)\n\n    # Move the window axis to be the last axis and compute median\n    window_axis = windowed.ndim - 1\n    result = np.median(windowed, axis=window_axis)\n\n    # Handle different modes\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return result\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        # Pad the result to have the same size as the input\n        pad_total = n - (n - window_size + 1)\n        pad_before = window_size // 2\n        pad_after = pad_total - pad_before\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        # Pad the result to have size n + window_size - 1\n        pad_total = window_size - 1\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = 0\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":6,"oldLines":6,"newStart":6,"newLines":7,"lines":[" import numpy as np"," from numpy._core import overrides"," from numpy._core.numeric import asarray, asanyarray","+from numpy._core.multiarray import normalize_axis_index"," "," __all__ = ['rolling_median']"," "]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

n + 1 elements\n            return np.broadcast_to(med, tuple(shape))\n\n    # Special case: window_size = 1\n    if window_size == 1:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a.astype(float if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Pad with NaN values\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = n\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Place the original values in the middle\n            slices = [slice(None)] * a.ndim\n            slices[axis] = slice(0, n)\n            result[tuple(slices)] = a\n            return result\n\n    # Compute rolling median using stride tricks\n    from numpy.lib.stride_tricks import sliding_window_view\n\n    # Create a sliding window view\n    windowed = sliding_window_view(a, window_size, axis=axis)\n\n    # The sliding_window_view adds a new axis at the end for the window\n    # We need to compute median along that axis\n    # The shape of windowed is: original_shape[:axis] + (n - window_size + 1,) + original_shape[axis+1:] + (window_size,)\n\n    # Move the window axis to be the last axis and compute median\n    window_axis = windowed.ndim - 1\n    result = np.median(windowed, axis=window_axis)\n\n    # Handle different modes\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        return result\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        # Pad the result to have the same size as the input\n        pad_total = n - (n - window_size + 1)\n        pad_before = window_size // 2\n        pad_after = pad_total - pad_before\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        # Pad the result to have size n + window_size - 1\n        pad_total = window_size - 1\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = 0\n\n        # Create padding tuple\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n\n        # Pad with NaN\n        return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":101,"oldLines":7,"newStart":101,"newLines":7,"lines":["         a = a.ravel()","         axis = 0"," ","-    axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)","+    axis = normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)"," ","     # Get the size along the specified axis","     n = a.shape[axis]"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

Since dtype should remain unchanged, we set it explicitly.\n104:     array.dtype = x.dtype\n105: \n106:     view = _maybe_view_as_subclass(x, array)\n107: \n108:     if view.flags.writeable and not writeable:\n109:         view.flags.writeable = False\n110: \n111:     return view\n112: \n113: \n114: def _sliding_window_view_dispatcher(x, window_shape, axis=None, *,\n115:                                     subok=None, writeable=None):\n116:     return (x,)\n117: \n118: \n119: @array_function_dispatch(\n120:     _sliding_window_view_dispatcher, module=\"numpy.lib.stride_tricks\"\n121: )\n122: def sliding_window_view(x, window_shape, axis=None, *,\n123:                         subok=False, writeable=False):\n124:     \"\"\"\n125:     Create a sliding window view into the array with the given window shape.\n126: \n127:     Also known as rolling or moving window, the window slides across all\n128:     dimensions of the array and extracts subsets of the array at all window\n129:     positions.\n130: \n131:     .. versionadded:: 1.20.0\n132: \n133:     Parameters\n134:     ----------\n135:     x : array_like\n136:         Array to create the sliding window view from.\n137:     window_shape : int or tuple of int\n138:         Size of window over each axis that takes part in the sliding window.\n139:         If `axis` is not present, must have same length as the number of input\n140:         array dimensions. Single integers `i` are treated as if they were the\n141:         tuple `(i,)`.\n142:     axis : int or tuple of int, optional\n143:         Axis or axes along which the sliding window is applied.\n144:         By default, the sliding window is applied to all axes and\n145:         `window_shape[i]` will refer to axis `i` of `x`.\n146:         If `axis` is given as a `tuple of int`, `window_shape[i]` will refer to\n147:         the axis `axis[i]` of `x`.\n148:         Single integers `i` are treated as if they were the tuple `(i,)`.\n149:     subok : bool, optional\n150:         If True, sub-classes will be passed-through, otherwise the returned\n151:         array will be forced to be a base-class array (default).\n152:     writeable : bool, optional\n153:         When true, allow writing to the returned view. The default is false,\n154:         as this should be used with caution: the returned view contains the\n155:         same memory location multiple times, so writing to one location will\n156:         cause others to change.\n157: \n158:     Returns\n159:     -------\n160:     view : ndarray\n161:         Sliding window view of the array. The sliding window dimensions are\n162:         inserted at the end, and the original dimensions are trimmed as\n163:         required by the size of the sliding window.\n164:         That is, ``view.shape = x_shape_trimmed + window_shape``, where\n165:         ``x_shape_trimmed`` is ``x.shape`` with every entry reduced by one less\n166:         than the corresponding window size.\n167: \n168:     See Also\n169:     --------\n170:     lib.stride_tricks.as_strided: A lower-level and less safe routine for\n171:         creating arbitrary views from custom shape and strides.\n172:     broadcast_to: broadcast an array to a given shape.\n173: \n174:     Notes\n175:     -----\n176:     For many applications using a sliding window view can be convenient, but\n177:     potentially very slow. Often specialized solutions exist, for example:\n178: \n179:     - `scipy.signal.fftconvolve`\n180: \n181:     - filtering functions in `scipy.ndimage`\n182: \n183:     - moving window functions provided by\n184:       `bottleneck <https://github.com/pydata/bottleneck>`_.\n185: \n186:     As a rough estimate, a sliding window approach with an input size of `N`\n187:     and a window size of `W` will scale as `O(N*W)` where frequently a special\n188:     algorithm can achieve `O(N)`. That means that the sliding window variant\n189:     for a window size of 100 can be a 100 times slower than a more specialized\n190:     version.\n191: \n192:     Nevertheless, for small window sizes, when no custom algorithm exists, or\n193:     as a prototyping and developing tool, this function can be a good solution.\n194: \n195:     Examples\n196:     --------\n197:     >>> import numpy as np\n198:     >>> from numpy.lib.stride_tricks import sliding_window_view\n199:     >>> x = np.arange(6)\n200:     >>> x.shape\n201: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/numpy--v2.2.2@9ca88bff35bf60de74f9f95e6f90e6b4e0913e78/-/blob/numpy/lib/_stride_tricks_impl.py%3FL90-200"}}}

Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output shape based on the window size and input array size:\n\n        'valid':\n            Output will have size max(N - window_size + 1, 0) where N is the\n            size along the given axis. This is the default mode.\n        'same':\n            Output will have the same shape as the input along the given axis.\n        'full':\n            Output will have size N + window_size - 1 where N is the size\n            along the given axis.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians. The output array has the same dtype as the\n        input array (or float64 for integer inputs less than 64-bit).\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    numpy.lib.stride_tricks.sliding_window_view : Create sliding windows.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed using a sliding window of the specified size.\n    For each window position, the median of the values in that window is computed.\n\n    The function handles edge cases as follows:\n    - If window_size is 1, the output is simply the input (in 'same' mode) or\n      a view of the input (in 'valid' or 'full' modes).\n    - If window_size is larger than the array size:\n      - 'valid' mode returns an empty array\n      - 'same' mode returns an array with NaN values\n      - 'full' mode returns the single median of the entire array\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 3, 6, 4, 5, 2])\n    >>> np.lib.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([3., 4., 4., 4.])\n\n    >>> a = np.array([[1, 2, 3, 4],\n    ... n + 1\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Compute median of the entire array along axis\n            med = np.median(a, axis=axis, keepdims=True)\n            # Reshape the result to have the window_size - n + 1 elements\n            return np.broadcast_to(med, tuple(shape))\n\n    # Special case: window_size = 1\n    if window_size == 1:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a.astype(float if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n        elif mode == 'full':\n            # Pad with NaN values\n            shape = list(a.shape)\n            shape[axis] = n\n            result = np.full(tuple(shape), np.nan, dtype=float)\n            # Place the original values in the middle\n            slices = [slice(None)] * a.ndim\n            slices[axis] = slice(0, n)\n            result[tuple(slices)] = a\n            return result\n\n    # Compute rolling median using stride tricks\n    from numpy.lib.stride_tricks import sliding_window_view\n\n    # Create a sliding window view\n    windowed = sliding_window_view(a, window_size, axis=axis)\n\n    # The sliding_window_view adds a new axis at the end for the window\n    # We need to compute median along that axis\n    # The shape of windowed is: original_shape[:axis] + (n - Rolling Median Implementation - Quick Reference\n\n## Files Created\n\n### Implementation File\n- **Location**: `/workspace/numpy/lib/_rolling_median_impl.py`\n- **Size**: ~6.5 KB\n- **Contents**:\n Parameters\n- `a`: array_like - Input array\n- `window_size`: int - Size of rolling window (must be ≥ 1)\n- `axis`: int - Axis along which to compute (default: -1)\n- `mode`: {'valid', 'same', 'full'} Input Conversion and Validation\n```python\na = asanyarray(a)  # Convert to NumPy array\n\n# Validate window_size\nif window_size < 1:\n    raise ValueError(\"window_size must be a positive integer\")\n\n# Validate mode\nif mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n    raise ValueError(f\"mode must be one of 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got {mode!r}\")\n```\n\n### 2. Axis Normalization\n```python\nif axis is None:\n    a = a.ravel()\n    axis = 0\n\naxis = normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\nn = a.shape[axis]\n```\n\n### 3. Edge Case: Window > Array\nHandled specially because sliding_window_view would fail:\n- **'valid'**: Return empty array with shape (0,) along axis\n- **'same'**: Return array of NaN values with input shape\n- **'full'**: Return array of NaN with shape (window_size - n + 1,) along axis\n\n### 4. Edge Case: Window Size = 1\nReturn a copy of the input (for 'valid'), converted to float (for 'same'), or padded (for 'full')\n\n### 5. Main Computation\n```python\nwindowed = sliding_window_view(a, window_size, axis=axis)\n# windowed shape: original_shape_trimmed + (window_size,)\n\nwindow_axis = windowed.ndim - 1\nresult = np.median(windowed, axis=window_axis)\n# result shape: original_shape_trimmed\n```\n\n### 6. Mode-Specific Padding\n\n#### Valid Mode (No Padding)\nSimply return the computed result as-is.\n\n#### Same Mode (Center Padding)\n```\npad_total = n - (n - window_size + 1) = window_size - 1\npad_before = window_size // 2\npad_after = pad_total - pad_before\nnp.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n```\n\nExample: window_size=3, n=5\n- pad_total = 2\n- pad_before = 1\n- pad_after = 1\n- Result: [NaN, median[0], median[1], median[2], NaN]\n\n#### Full Mode (Symmetric Padding)\n```\nfull_size = n + window_size - 1\ncurrent_size = n - window_size + 1\npad_before = window_size - 1\npad_after = window_size - 1\nnp.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n```\n\nExample: window_size=3, n=5\n- full_size = 7\n- current_size = 3\n- pad_before = 2\n- pad_after = 2\n- Result: [NaN, NaN, median[0], median[1], median[2], NaN, NaN]\n\n## Data Type Handling\n\n- Input arrays are accepted as-is via `asanyarray`\n- Integer arrays are typically converted to float by `np.median`\n- Output preserves NumPy's median dtype convention\n- NaN padding uses `np.nan` (float)\n\n## Array Function Dispatch\n\nThe `@array_function_dispatch` decorator enables:\n1. Subclass support (e.g., `np.ma.array`, custom array types)\n2. Proper dispatch through NumPy's `__array_function__` protocol\n3. Automatic handling of ndarray subclasses\n\nDispatcher function:\n```python\ndef _rolling_median_dispatcher(a, window_size, axis=None, mode=None):\n    return (a,)  # Only 'a' participates in dispatch\n```\n\n## Performance Characteristics\n\n- **Time Complexity**: O(N * W * log(W)) where N is array size and W is window size\n  - N windows\n  - Computing median of W elements: O(W * log(W)) using NumPy's median\n- **Space Complexity**: O(N * W) due to sliding window view\n- **Memory Efficiency**: Uses stride tricks (view-based, not copying)\n\n## Error Handling\n\n1. **ValueError: invalid window_size**\n   - window_size < 1\n\n2. **ValueError: invalid mode**\n   - mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full')\n\n3. **Implicit errors** (from NumPy functions):\n   - Invalid axis (handled by `normalize_axis_index`)\n   - Non-numeric input (from `asanyarray`)\n\n## Comparison with NumPy Functions\n\n| Function | Input | Window | Mode | Padding |\n|----------|-------|--------|------|---------|\n| `rolling_median` | 1-D to N-D | Explicit | Explicit | NaN |\n| `np.convolve` | 1-D | Explicit | Explicit | Implicit |\n| `np.correlate` | 1-D | Explicit | Explicit | Implicit |\n| `np.median` | Any-D | None (reduce) | None | None |\n\n## Testing Strategy\n\n### Unit Test Categories\n\n1. **Basic Functionality**\n   - Correct median computation\n   - Different window sizes\n   - Different input types\n\n2. **Mode Testing**\n   - Each mode produces correct shapes\n   - Padding with NaN in 'same' and 'full'\n   - Invalid modes raise errors\n\n3. **Edge Cases**\n   - window_size > array length\n   - window_size = 1\n   - Empty arrays\n   - Single element arrays\n\n4. **Dimensional Support**\n   - 1D, 2D, 3D arrays\n   - All axes (positive and negative)\n   - Shape preservation in 'same' mode\n\n5. **Data Type Support**\n   - Integer arrays\n   - Float arrays\n   - Complex numbers (if median supports)\n   - Mixed precision\n\n6. **Subclass Support**\n   - NumPy array subclasses\n   - Proper dispatch behavior\n\n## Known Limitations\n\n1. **Performance for Large Windows**: O(N*W) complexity may be slow for large W\n   - Alternative: Use rolling window library or implement using deques\n\n2. **NaN Handling**: `np.median` behavior with NaN varies by NumPy version\n   - Some versions ignore NaN, others propagate it\n   - Test suite is flexible to account for this\n\n3. **Memory Usage**: For large arrays with large windows, memory usage is O(N*W)\n   - Could be optimized with streaming algorithms\n\n4. **Single Axis Only**: Unlike NumPy's axis parameter (tuple), this works on one axis\n   - Could be extended to support multiple axes\n\n## Future Enhancements\n\n1. **Custom Median Implementations**\n   - For integer data, use radix-based algorithms\n   - For partially sorted data, use optimized quickselect\n\n2. **Alternative Modes**\n   -
